< Review>
A traditional Italian menu set in a modern space. You can tell the love and care put into each dish and the warning on the menu speaks volumes to ensuring they don't sacrifice the quality by saying if it is busy orders can take up to 40 minutes as everything is made from scratch. If you can't afford to take some time to appreciate the care they put in then come early or come later in the evening.

And while the food is fantastic, the hospitality is equally attentive. This night due to a glitch one order did not come the same time as the rest of our dishes. The service recovery was beyond excellent as they gave the kids a little treat to make up for it. This was on top of attending to a wobbly table and constantly coming by to ensure we were always topped up with bread or ensuring we were done with our dishes. Highly recommend this restaurant.</Review>

< text>
Terrible food at a high price point with mediocre service. No idea how this place has a 4.3 star rating.
The best thing about this place is it's location. In fact, that might be the only good thing about this place.
To be fair, the guy who greeted us and showed us to our table was very friendly.
Unfortunately, he was not our waiter and we never saw him again.
Our "service," if you can call it that, was taken over by a woman who  was extremely direct, unfriendly, and lacked any kind of warmth or personable qualities.
It's okay if you hate people, lady, but maybe choose a different profession.

She-who-hates-people-and-should-not-be-waiting-tables came to take our order 20 minutes after we sat down.
She brought, hands down, the most awful bread I have ever been served in a restaurant.
It literally tastes like it was made with 1950's Bisquick mix: kinda crumbly in the middle with a weak, somewhat dampish "crust."
This was served with an oily canned tomato concoction with some basil and garlic mixed in. Somehow this failed to disguise the depressing quality and bitter disappointment of the bisquick bread.
What kind of Authentic Italian restaurant serves Bisquick bread?!!!
Do they even have Bisquick in Italy?
Next I made the horrific mistake of ordering the Gorgonzola and Smoked Salmon Bruschetta, not thinking for a moment that it would be served on, you guessed it, Bisquick bread!
For $15.50 you too can have the most unimaginably anemic smear of watery Gorgonzola under a bit of store bought smoked salmon on top of bisquick bread. Step right up!
The mixed green with beet salad was borderline fresh. The greens weren't rotten, but they weren't winning any awards for perkiness. Maybe they wilted in the presence of our fair host. I'm pretty sure the beets came out of a can and the rasberry dressing was most likely costco brand. Not very good.
My recommendation: order this salad with no greens, no dressing, and no beets.
Just ask for a bowl of candied walnuts and save yourself the disappointment.
Next came the Gorgonzola Gnocci which, by comparison to the rest of the meal, didn't completely suck, though, the low quality of the rest of meal did lend itself to skepticism about whether the Gnocci and it's respective sauce also came from the freezer section at costco.
We were too terrified of further disappointment to order dessert.
Overall, the best part of this entire experience was leaving knowing we never have to repeat this experience again.
There are so many fantastic restaurants in Carlsbad. This is not one of them.</text>

<Review>What was supposed to be a simple evening of Italian food and a few drinks quickly became an experience to remember for all the wrong reasons. It all started quite well honestly, the two of us were walk-ins after the dinner rush around 2000 (8pm). We were sat at a small table, good atmosphere and what started as a very promising dining experience began; oh how wrong we were!
It began with waters and bread, no complaints there (perhaps the only thing that went right). We promptly ordered drinks and one of the calamari appetizers. Simple enough one would think... Our drinks arrived about ten minutes later and we ordered our meals. One Moscow Mule and one Margarita. The Moscow Mule was terrible, it was made with Gin... a Moscow Mule with gin... really? You‚Äôd think as it‚Äôs offered as a special the bar staff would have had it mastered, apparently that was too much to ask. The margarita was good so perhaps a win for the bartender there, until I reordered.... it was in a tall glass with three extra limes in what I‚Äôm assuming was filler to ensure the liquid met the brim of the glass. It also tasted heavily diluted the second time and not the same color as the first one. Class act.
At this point the main course came out. Yes, before the calamari. We notified the staff that we would no longer like the calamari which they were somewhat understanding of. Somewhat. Our very young looking male server had an attitude when we addressed it with him. Then proceed to not come back to the table until 30 minutes after we were obviously done with our meals, plates cleared and we were trying to get is attention (without bothering other guests).
Overall as a new resident of the area I would strongly recommended you seek another restaurant to have your evening out at. As someone who comes from a background in the food and beverage industry, I would be embarrassed if this were to happen in an establishment where I worked or represented. Again, foodies seek other eateries around town, not worth the time or money. Owner, consider new management, the manager appeared to be spending the majority of his time at a barstool rather than tending to the restaurant.

< Review>
Delicious food! Started with warm bread and chilled homemade marinara for dipping (chunks of tomato, seasoned with basil, garlic vinegar and olive oil) then graduated to the pappardelle pasta with lobster cream sauce, shrimp and diver scallops (with red bell pepper and zucchini for added color and flavor).  You can get this dish anytime, even if it's not actually on the menu at the time of your visit (it's that popular). I added a fresh 5 oz lobster tail and wasn't disappointed! My husband had the seafood lasagne (crab, seabass, salmon) which was a big hit as well and ordered two glasses of wine. We didn't order dessert and I just drank water but the bill was over $100 so it's not a place I would go on a regular basis but for a special occasion it's a great option.</Review>

<userid>105429266873887922483</userid>< name>
Richard Nelson< /name>
<Time>1513887591335</Time>< Rating>
2< /Rating>
<Text>I cannot understand why people rant and rave about this place.  It's okay, but certainly nothing special.  Perhaps those doing the rating and raving haven't been anywhere else?

My wife and I like the joint for a place to have a glass of wine on the patio near the sidewalk.  We find that the wait staff is very nice and very good.

The food?  For us that's another story.  We find it to be mediocre at best.  On the evening of 12/08/17, we ordered fettuccine alfredo with crab meat.  Remember the Wendy's commercial from years ago which exclaimed, "Where's the beef?"  After dining at Ciocotti's, our question is, "Where's the crab?"  This is not to say that the fettuccine was devoid of crab.  Believe it or not, there were actually some bits and pieces of crab mixed in.  We had to use a magnifying glass to find them, but they were there.

I understand that dining out is expensive and that Ciocotti's is not bashful in presenting you with a three digit bill.  But, for goodness sake, if you are going to charge a premium price for a few noodles with alfredo sauce and microscopic pieces of crab, at least include a hefty portion of crab not unlike that which you get at Fisherman's Wharf in San Francisco.

Bottom line?  We will return to Ciocotti's for a glass of wine or two, but don't bother to bring us the food menu.</Text>< Pics>
None<//Pics>

< text>
Love this San Francisco iconic yarn store.
Absolutely packed to the brim with an amazing selection of yarns, I could easily spend 2 hours just working on colourscapes for future projects.
The library is very well stocked with books well beyond patterns.
Many notions available and some unusual pieces I had been looking for.
The staff were incredibly helpful and went out of their way to ensure I got exactly what I needed for my project.
Regular classes available as well as fun knit alongs. Keep your eyes out as many celebrity knitters have been known to stop by.< /text>

< text>
This is the place to go if you're looking for a large selection! A little overwhelming at first, but once you figure out how its organized (first room is wools, and the other is acrylics, cottons, silks, linens, etc) then it becomes easier to find what you want. It's great that you can find the normal stuff that most yarn shops carry in addition to things that many yarn shops don't. Very easy to find something unique (esp if you're visiting from elsewhere). Wasn't super impressed with the customer service, but did like that I wasn't bugged by everyone. Overall a good experience, just wish the staff was a little friendlier and more welcoming.</text>

< Text>
An adorable little shop in the Castro district of SF, which means: Men working in a knitting store! The people here are so sweet and helpful. I really didn't need any more yarn, but dang it, they had a bunch of cool knitting/project bags and totes that called my name. But if I were looking for yarn, there are skeins and skeins of drool-worthy fibers packed in cubbies from floor to ceiling, and they're arranged by weight, going in a counterclockwise direction throughout the store. So you start with your lace weight when you walk in the door and end with the bulky weights at the end. There's also a selection of knitting tools as well as knitting-related impulse items to wring the $$ out of any self-respecting knitter. They offer classes here too so it's a full-service knitting store. Whether you're just thinking of getting into knitting or are an expert, you'll find something here to intrigue you. Oh, and they let me use their bathroom--double plus good!</Text>

< review>
I just started to learn to knit and wanted to check out a yarn store in the neighborhood and could help me pick out the right yarn and tools for a fingerless glove project.
The people at the store were very helpful in explaining the outlay of their yarn collection and were so excited for me and my project using a specific yarn.  Little did I know

organic meat for cooking. Not sure I would buy everything here since there are cheaper places and I'm not sure they have an exchange policy, but it's a good start for a newbie knitter.</review>

< date>

<Gmap_id>0x808f9dda44dfe47d:0x55ae98ca132e0d47</Gmap_id><UserId.>109688448148639634910< /UserId.><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Review>
I arrived at about 16:15 on a Friday, end of month (Jan 31) and was out of there by 17:30. I went in to resolve a demand for payment issue regarding my vehicle registration.

The non-appointment line flowed very quickly, I was in it only for about 15/20 minutes. The concierge helped me and provided me a number. I then sat in the waiting area for another 20 minutes or so.

When I was called, the agent who helped me was very friendly. I didn't catch his name but he was male, and was nice - chatted go Niners with me for a minute since this was the weekend before the Superbowl.

His computer froze on him, so he could not help me resolve my issue, but we walked me to another window and explained the situation to the female agent who was there - she was also very friendly.

They did have a processing issue with some notes on my account (I was supposed to get a discount that, of course, did not show in their system). I just paid in full, though, and they provided me paperwork to apply for a refund to get the discount thing sorted.

Last step was to confirm that the flag on my account was removed. Unfortunately, it wasn't and it was after 17:00 so they couldn't get in touch with Sacramento to confirm. However, this is why they get a 5-star review: they took down my information and told me they would take care of all this on Monday morning without me having to come back in, provided me full receipts and account numbers and backup paperwork so I could call myself, and provided me free of charge a temporary operating permit for a full 30 days so I could have peace of mind in operating my vehicle!

Thank you, DMV team, for making what is usually always a horror story a really, really positive experience.</Review>

Non appointments line up on the west side of the building easy to notice by the long line of people.. Also there is no parking onsite as the gates to the parking lot are closed until 8am. 7am opens, but line forms at back, West door.
Expect at least a 30 min Standing wait in line. 40 outdoor chairs would be nice.
Very few DMV employees at opening hour.
Bring a jacket and hat.
And a light little walker with a seat if you have one!

The clerk at the head of the line before the counter has too small a desk for paperwork and is too slow.

Here to renew my DL and had to fill out an online Application to Renew a DL, since they only mailed me the Notice to Renew.

The terminal on the left corner is too shaky and hard to fill out.
Use the keypad for 8 digit birthday, not the on-screen scroll arrows.
Another 15minutes...

Clerk at Window #5 forgot my SSA card was still under the cover of the printer... for about 15min.

The clock on the back wall is too small, unlit, and too hard to read from the front, with 20/20 vision.
Waiting in the front main seating area...
Probably another 30min...
Bathroom is behind us.
Is that old harsh florescent tube ceiling lighting??

Waiting to take Written Test.
Then Fingerprint and Photo.
Only one chair for Handicaps test taking;
What about us old Senior Citizens with canes and bad knees?

If you have Any Commercial issues, try to go to the Mtn View Commercial DMV office instead.

Wish they would stop using hooked 6s and hooked 9s.
And 3s that look like 8s.

9:15am,,,2 hours,,,still waiting,,,

No mirror below or near the camera ,,,so you know how much to smile! Tsk tsk.

Most Employees do not wear a necklace ID badge, just 1guy did.

Also the "submit" button is too thin and did not work several times.
All screens should have chairs.
Only one low Handicap screen with chair!

10:15am,,,3hrs 15min,,, still waiting, after Photo, Fingerprint(works better if you hold it in your left hand), and 18 question DL Renew License Test.

My fav fastest DMV office is hwy 24x680, then also small Santa Teresa in SJ.
Avoid Golden Gate Park location and Fremont!!

6Feb2020, got my new high security DL in a week!
But it's the Worst color photo ever! All yellow!
Just something else DMV needs to fix!<//text>

<Rating>4< /Rating>< Text>
Considering this is the DMV, and the entire system is horrendously outdated and inefficient, I was quite satisfied with my experience at this branch.  I had no appointment, so showed up at 6:40 with a line of some 15 people.  I was pleased and surprised when the doors opened early at 7:30.  We were greeted and directed to the appropriate line and given slips of paper to expedite the check-in process.

I was inside by 8:00 and was directed to a small kiosk where a helpful gentleman assisted people. He pointed us to the right line where we them received our queue number.  The line was short and I had my number in about 15 minutes.  After this it was a mere 10 minutes more until my number was called.

I was greeted cordially and asked if I had my documents ready.  Since I was doing a license renewal, they needed things like a passport, SS card or 401k, etc.  The process took another 10 minutes and was pain free.  The representative was courteous and dutiful.

Finally I was directed to the picture line to get the new photo (hoping it turned out well) and that was it!  I was out by 8:40.

Despite the outdated system, the workers made this place tick.  None seemed stressed or overworked which was refreshing, and I never felt silly for asking questions.

Bottom line, avood going in person if you can, but if you must, make an appointment (2 months in advance).  If you don't have an appointment, come here at least 90 minutes before they open and you should have a pretty painless experience.  Bring a lawn chair and snacks if you come later because your non-apppintment wait time will exponentially increase the later you arrive (see my SF DMV review).<//Text>

< Rating>

<review>This place is extremely crowded. However, it is relatively less crowded than the other nearby DMVs (Redwood city). After reading the other reviews, I decided its better to get their early and wait in the early morning, which would then get me ahead in the waiting line (before doors open). Note that the parking lot opens only at 8 am. Hence, you will be parking on the roadside. Note that there is street cleaning on 2nd and 4th Tuesdays from 10 to noon (I think). So make sure you are done by then. Also note the DMV opens at 9 am on Wednesdays and 8 am on the rest of the days. I think Thursday is relatively less crowded. I was there at 6:10 am. I was 3rd in line :-) At 7:45 am a gentleman comes out of the DMV office and splits the people waiting in two lines. One on the left for non license renewals and the one on the right for license renewals. For license renewals he also provides a link to fill out an online application form - I advice in doing this a day prior and taking a print out of the conf number of the online form. They open the doors at 8 am. The left most line (C - I think) is for license renewals. I got counter 7 with no wait time and was done in 10 minutes - eye test, photos taken, right thumb print taken, fees paid via debit card. Note that the $35 fees for license renewal is by cash, check or debit card - no credit cards. The lady in the counter was thorough, courteous and efficient. Overall, it helps to be prepared of lines and delays.</review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Resp>

Compared to the DMV offices in San Francisco and in Daly City, the San Mateo location is by far the quickest moving and the best one for last minute visits.  Of course make an appointment online when possible, but life happens and we don't all make appointments.  I was off on a weekday and needed to have my photo taken for a new driver's license.  I live closest to the Daly City location.  I checked the DMV site online and found that the DC wait time was much shorter than SF.  I drove to Daly City without an appointment and couldn't even park.  There was a long line out the door.  I decided to drive farther to San Mateo.  There was plenty of parking and no line out the door.  I got into a short line, waited briefly, had a new photo taken and was out the door in less than half an hour.</review>
